            <div class="article-inner-container" style="max-width:1280px;">
             <div class="inset-container Mx-a">
              <div class="GridTable">
               <div class="D-tbr row-template">
                <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left">

                   <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-119035119448">
                      Alarming Consumer Reports Study: Your Sunscreen May Not Work
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-119035119448" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="D-b Fs-n Pb-14 byline col">
                           <span class="D-b author-name col-left">
                            <a class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-b" data-action-outcome="navigate" data-routable-url="/beauty/author/sara-bliss" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:8f5f71cf-f799-311c-99db-f771fa3cce2e;t9:16;elm:itm;elmt:cat;itc:0" href="/beauty/author/sara-bliss" rel="author" style="color:#000;">
                             Sara Bliss
                            </a>
                           </span>
                           <span class="D-b Font-C-2-140 Fw-n author-title">
                            Senior Writer
                           </span>
                           <time class="D-b Font-C-2-140 Fw-n date">
                            <span>
                             May 25, 2015
                            </span>
                           </time>
                           <div class="follow Mt-4">
                            <iframe allowtransparency="true" frameborder="0" scrolling="no" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets/follow_button.html?screen_name=sarablissnyc&amp;show_screen_name=false&amp;show_count=false" style="border:none;overflow:hidden;width:60px;height:20px;">
                            </iframe>
                           </div>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t Va-b" style="width:133px;">
                          <a class="attribution-photo author-photo-link col" data-action-outcome="navigate" data-routable-url="/beauty/author/sara-bliss" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:8f5f71cf-f799-311c-99db-f771fa3cce2e;t9:16;elm:itm;elmt:cat;itc:0" href="/beauty/author/sara-bliss">
                           <img alt="Sara Bliss" class="author-photo" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w133/9a65dd5b0289830ca9554d0edad8cf3f68dd2e64.png" style="width:133px;"/>
                          </a>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-119035119448" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <figure>
                          <img alt="Alarming Consumer Reports Study: Your Sunscreen May Not Work" height="698" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w540/b0f1f48daa6e8bd763488cd28b3a10aa6ed7ad80.jpg" width="540"/>
                         </figure>
                         <p>
                          <i>
                           Find out which sunscreens you should use and which to avoid.
                          </i>
                          (
                          <i>
                           Photo: David Burton/Trunk Archive)
                          </i>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          In an alarming new study by
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:8f5f71cf-f799-311c-99db-f771fa3cce2e;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.consumerreports.org/cro/sunscreens.htm" target="_blank">
                           Consumer Reports
                          </a>
                          , one third of sunscreens tested didnt offer the protection promised on their labels. Out of the 34 sunscreens put to the test, 11 failed to meet their SPF and water-resistant claims.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The watchdog group focused particularly on how sunscreens hold up against UVA and UVB rays after they have been exposed to water. They sampled a wide range of price points from drugstore brands to fancy European suncare. To see how the sunscreens held up, they were applied to testers backs, and submerged in water for the amount of time that the sunscreen promised to hold up. For example, if the product claimed to be waterproof for an hour, that is how long testers would stay drenched. Afterwards testers were exposed to an ultra violet light to determine the effectiveness of the product against the suns rays.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The 11 sunscreens that didnt live up to expectations missed their target by anywhere from 16% to 70%. Interestingly, 8 of the 11 had an SPF below 30. While its clear an SPF 30 or above is a good target to look for, dont be fooled into thinking SPFs of 50 or above is always going to add a ton of protection. Several of the high SPF products dont offer as much SPF as they claim. Coppertone ClearlySheer for Beach &amp; Pool SPF 50+ tested as an SPF 37, and Banana Boat Sport Performance with Powerstay Technology SPF 100 tested as an SPF 36.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The other red flag brought up by the study was about natural sunscreens, pointing out that the word natural means nothing on a label. They do acknowledge that it is often used to refer to products that contain zinc oxide and/or titanium dioxide as active ingredients. Consumer Reports states that so-called naturals are less likely to offer skin the complete protection it needs. They tested five mineral sunscreens and three failed. Of the two that did meet their SPF claim, neither received enough high scores to be recommended including California Baby Super Sensitive SPF 30+, and Goddess Garden Organics Sunny Body Natural 30.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          However, while the study is alarming, its worth noting that the test was really focused on how sunscreens hold up in water, which may not be a fair test. Given that we tell people to reapply sunscreen when coming out of the water, you should look at this study with caution, says Manhattan-based dermatologist Dr. Sejal Shah. Ultimately, the study should be a reminder that sunscreen alone, isnt the best protection. If you are going in the water wear a rash guard. If you are outside, wear sun protective clothing, a hat, and sunglasses too, explains dermatologist Dr. Ava Shamban. Remember, sunscreen is not the end all be all. Dont stop using it, but use other forms of protection too.
                          <br/>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Here are the sunscreens that earned the top ratings:
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          1. La Roche-Posay Anthelios 60 Melt-in Sunscreen Milk, SPF 60.
                          <br/>
                          2. Vichy Capital Soleil 50 Lightweight Foaming Lotion, SPF 50
                          <br/>
                          3. Coppertone Water Babies SPF 50
                          <br/>
                          4. Equate Ultra Protection, SPF 50
                          <br/>
                          5. No-Ad Sport SPF 50
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Here are the sunscreens that earned the lowest ratings:
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          1. Vanicream SPF 50
                          <br/>
                          2. Goddess Garden Organics Sunny Body Natural 30
                          <br/>
                          3. Yes to Cucumbers Natural SPF 30
                          <br/>
                          4. Elta MD UV Aero SPF 45
                          <br/>
                          5. Aloe Gator SPF 40
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:999999px;max-width:500px;">
                         <p>
                          <b>
                           <i>
                            Related:
                           </i>
                          </b>
                         </p>

                           <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:8f5f71cf-f799-311c-99db-f771fa3cce2e;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/beauty/the-history-of-sunscreen-117797098013.html" target="_blank">

Constance Zimmer on Why She Loves Playing Badass Women","summary":"Constance Zimmer stars as Quinn King, the strong, confident, and often-ruthless executive producer of the fictitious show Everlasting. Its not the first time Zimmer has played a badass woman  she portrayed movie executive Dana Gordon on Entourage (she recently reunited with the cast for the film version) and journalist Janine Skorsky on House of Cards  but her newest character might be her best yet.  We caught up with Zimmer to talk reality television, her love of face masks, and what we can expect from season two of UnReal.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F0efc9f01ff6ef4f1eb450210c02364fac51588fd.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"626\" alt=\"UnReal&#x2019;s Constance Zimmer on Why She Loves Playing Badass Women\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EActress Constance Zimmer stars in the new TV series UnReal. (Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf you love \u003Ci\u003EThe Bachelorette\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, you have to tune in to \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.mylifetime.com\u002Fshows\u002Funreal\"\u003EUnReal\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, a new Lifetime series that follows a team of producers as they create a dating competition program. \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002Fconstancezimmer\"\u003EConstance Zimmer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E stars as Quinn King, the strong, confident, and often-ruthless executive producer of the fictitious show &#x201C;Everlasting.&#x201D; It&#x2019;s not the first time Zimmer has played a badass woman &#x2014; she portrayed movie executive Dana Gordon on \u003Ci\u003EEntourage\u003C\u002Fi\u003E (she recently reunited with the cast for the film version) and journalist Janine Skorsky on \u003Ci\u003EHouse of Cards\u003C\u002Fi\u003E &#x2014; but her newest character might be her best yet. We caught up with Zimmer to talk reality television, her love of face masks, and what we can expect from season two of \u003Ci\u003EUnReal\u003C\u002Fi\u003E.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EAlexandra Perron: I&#x2019;m so excited that we could jump on the phone today. I&#x2019;ve been watching UnREAL, and because I&#x2019;m a shameless fan of The Bachelor, I&#x2019;m totally addicted to the show.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EConstance Zimmer: Oh good.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EI think your character, Quinn, is a total a badass, she&#x2019;s really smart, and she&#x2019;s really tough. You&#x2019;ve played roles like this in the past, on Entourage and House of Cards. What&#x2019;s it like portraying really strong, tough women?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m super proud to be able to portray them and that there are so many on my resume that I&#x2019;ve been able to do on different levels &#x2014; political levels and entertainment levels. These strong women exist everywhere, but when they&#x2019;re portrayed on television they&#x2019;re always played to an extreme to make a point. So, for me, what I always try and make sure that we&#x2019;re all doing from a writing and acting stand point and the story stand point, is to make sure that they&#x2019;re not just one color &#x2014; because nobody is just one color. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI think Quinn, and I hate to use this word, is the quintessential example of the person who does such a good job of separating her career, her business, who she is at work, from what her personal life is. In this kind of world where she&#x2019;s producing reality television and she&#x2019;s producing people&#x2019;s lives, I think it forces her to not look at her own love life. Which is why her love life is such a mess. Which is why it&#x2019;s been so much fun to portray her in particular; because a lot of her strengths or anger toward the situation comes form her own experience.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYeah, and we have seen a few moments where she&#x2019;s been really vulnerable and let her guard down. It&#x2019;s so important that she&#x2019;s still really strong, but also shows that she&#x2019;s human throughout the show. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EQuinn is the first character that I&#x2019;ve played where you get to see all of her. Dana was a reoccurring character and we didn&#x2019;t get to see much of her personal life, and Janine the same thing. So with Quinn it&#x2019;s been so fun, because we&#x2019;ve been allowed to dive into her personal life.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fec0de9876d7d34215f85aef5b90a4cc1984399a8.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EZimmer as Quinn King with her team of producers in an episode of UnReal. (Photo: James Dittiger)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe show on UnREAL, &#x201C;Everlasting,&#x201D; was obviously based on these Bachelor-style dating shows. Did you watch any of them leading up to the show or do you watch them now? \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI do sort of watch them as an outline to understand this kind of thing, to be aware of it. I just wanted to have the same awareness as everyone else.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EDo you have a reality show guilty pleasure? \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAmazing Race. I love that show. I also watch Project Runway. Those kinds of reality shows, to me, were easier to watch &#x2014; the drama felt like a second story line, whereas the dating shows, those feel like the drama is the first story line. I don&#x2019;t know if you really learn anything from those types of shows. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EShiri [Appleby] and I were just celebrity judges on Project Runway.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EOh awesome!\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWe did it last week. It was funny; Shiri said to me, &#x201C;I think we just got produced.&#x201D; It was so fun being on a reality show after working on our show. It&#x2019;s like, wait, did they just make us say that? Are they going to edit us down to sound meaner than we did?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EA lot of the contestants on &#x201C;Everlasting&#x201D; come onto the show with so much confidence, but the producers break them down and they lose that confidence. What have you learned about confidence over the years? \u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor me, it&#x2019;s always having a sense of self. And knowing who you really are when you&#x2019;re at home, not when you&#x2019;re in front of a crew or in front of a camera. It really helps to keep me balanced. It&#x2019;s very easy to become insecure and upset. I&#x2019;ve also been super blessed to play really strong confident women &#x2014; it actually forces me to always be above and beyond who I am. I&#x2019;m not as strong or as confident as the characters that I play, but the one thing I&#x2019;m confident about, is just who I am as a person. And I don&#x2019;t ever let somebody dictate that, that will never change. I can definitely go from being super soft and vulnerable to being incredibly strong and sassy and all of that, but ultimately it just comes from having your core be really strong and not letting anybody else tell you otherwise. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ENow that UnREAL has been picked up for another season, is there anything that we can expect from the second season? Is it going to be another &#x201C;Everlasting,&#x201D; is it going to be another reality show?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYeah, from what we&#x2019;ve been told, which is not much, the show &#x201C;Everlasting&#x201D; will be everlasting, but the situations might be different. For example, it might not be a suitor and 25 women &#x2014; it might be a female looking for love and 25 men, [or] it could be a man and a woman. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fe9ec2bd2f7087a969f1db1ad00e363a8e5d76a83.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EUnReal stars Shiri Appleby (left) and Constance Zimmer (right). (Photo: Joseph Viles)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELet&#x2019;s switch gears and talk about your beauty routine. In all of your years acting, what have you learned about beauty?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s such a tricky thing because you get introduced to new products all the time. So you quickly try and figure out what works for you, but you&#x2019;re traveling a lot and you&#x2019;re stressed out, so different products work for you at different times. It almost comes down to the inside out &#x2014; drinking a lot of water, having cold pressed juices once or twice a day &#x2014; and finding those beauty products that work for different times in your life. When you&#x2019;re working, your beauty regimen is so much different because of all the stuff that is being put on your face everyday. Keeping yourself feeling hydrated and never allowing your skin to get dry has always been the most important thing. Body lotion, face lotion, and eye cream. And lately I&#x2019;m obsessed with these amazing face masks.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWhich face masks do you like?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe ones from Tatcha. You put it over your whole face and you leave it on for like half an hour. And I&#x2019;ve found that if you do that like every other week, it&#x2019;s amazing how much it hydrates and moisturizes your skin. And they have just the little eye ones, too &#x2014; I do those before I get my makeup done.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWhat&#x2019;s your off-camera beauty vibe? Do you pamper yourself?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m very low key. I probably should be more high-maintenance, [but] it&#x2019;s an expense that I&#x2019;ve never allowed myself. If I&#x2019;m not working then I&#x2019;m trying to save myself time by sleeping and spending time with my family. The idea of going and leaving for three hours to go and be pampered is just is a tough choice for me. Next Friday I&#x2019;m going in for a facial, because it&#x2019;s like, OK, six months of traveling and press and all that, I think I finally deserve something. It&#x2019;s hard to find the time without feeling guilty.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDo you know Ren&#xE9; Rouleau? She&#x2019;s awesome because she&#x2019;s one of those people where her products make the facials, but it&#x2019;s not a facial itself. She makes it like a whole schedule for me. She has this awesome toner that I use every night. Her lotions are so specific to me, which I like, because there&#x2019;s not just one. And I really love serums.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThey are so nourishing and you feel the impact of them immediately because they penetrate so well and they&#x2019;re full of so many actives. It&#x2019;s like the best drink for your skin, a good serum.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd you know what&#x2019;s great, too, is Beauty Counter.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EI love Beauty Counter!\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYes and it&#x2019;s completely terrifying when you realize that probably half the stuff in your cabinet has horrible ingredients. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EIt&#x2019;s the worst realization, especially as a beauty editor, because I have so many products and I don&#x2019;t want to put any of it on my face anymore! It&#x2019;s so scary.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EYeah, but you know, good for them. Maybe that&#x2019;s why I&#x2019;m playing these characters, but I&#x2019;m all for people just saying, &#x201C;We&#x2019;re being honest and do what you want.&#x201D; Some people will say, &#x201C;I&#x2019;m still going to use these because they&#x2019;re good for my skin.&#x201D; Which is fine, you know, we all should. And then there are people that really, really care and want to know what is in their products. Kylie Jenner's Cornrows Sparked Outrage","summary":"Just this past weekend, the reality star posted a photo of herself on Instagram sporting cornrows with the caption, I woke up like disss. And thats when the fighting began.  Hunger Games actress Amandla Stenberg claimed that Jenner was appropriating Black culture by sporting the hairstyle without doing anything to help the community.  Some people said she should be able to wear whatever hairstyle she wants to, regardless of culture.  Some pointed out that someone could easily point to black women wearing wigs and extensions of European texture as cultural appropriation (the adoption of elements of one culture by a different cultural group).","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fc72595ef55c5017c53529a69770a1dc163934c21.png\" alt=\"Why Kylie Jenner&apos;s Cornrows Sparked Outrage\" width=\"540\" height=\"495\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EKylie Jenner sporting cornrow braids. (Photo: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Finstagram.com\u002Fkyliejenner\u002F\"\u003EInstagram\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt seems the Kardashian-Jenner family is never out of the news for one reason or another, and the new frequent center of the attention is youngest sibling, Kylie Jenner. Just this past weekend, the reality star \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bbc.co.uk\u002Fnewsbeat\u002Farticle\u002F33503069\u002Fkylie-jenners-hair-cause\"\u003Eposted a photo of herself on Instagram\u003C\u002Fa\u003E sporting cornrows with the caption, &#x201C;I woke up like disss.&#x201D; And that&#x2019;s when the fighting began. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EHunger Games\u003C\u002Fi\u003E actress Amandla Stenberg \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.huffingtonpost.com\u002Fentry\u002Famandla-\"\u003Eclaimed that Jenner was &#x201C;appropriating Black culture&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E by sporting the hairstyle without doing anything to help the community. Jenner said that was not her intention, and the melee began on social media. Some people said she should be able to wear whatever hairstyle she wants to, regardless of culture. Some pointed out that someone could easily point to black women wearing wigs and extensions of European texture as cultural appropriation (the adoption of elements of one culture by a different cultural group). Others claimed that the wounds go much deeper than just the hairstyle.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut Stenberg, who crafted the video &#x201C;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=O1KJRRSB_XA\"\u003EDon&#x2019;t Cash Crop My Cornrows\u003C\u002Fa\u003E,&#x201D; raises a very interesting point in regards to such matters: &#x201C;What if America loved Black people as much as it loves Black culture?&#x201D; At a time where racial tensions have reached heights that haven&#x2019;t been seen in almost 50 years, it&#x2019;s time to think about what messages people with a platform are sending when they just grab something from another culture because it looks cool. The discussion could get pretty big here: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theroot.com\u002Fblogs\u002Fthe_grapevine\u002F2014\u002F07\u002Fkaty_the_queen_of_cultural_appropri\"\u003EKaty Perry\u003C\u002Fa\u003E dressing up like a geisha in her videos, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fjezebel.com\u002Fon-miley-cyrus-ratchet-culture-and-accessorizing-with-514381016\"\u003EMiley Cyrus\u003C\u002Fa\u003E using black backup dancers and grills as accessories in prior videos. There&#x2019;s a never-ending list of Caucasians using black style without giving any credit to the culture from whence it came. The sensitivity around Jenner came from her sporting cornrows and a hip hop-influenced stance without any accreditation to the culture that created that look. It&#x2019;s not that she shouldn&#x2019;t be able to wear the hairstyle, but maybe use the platform to educate folks a little?\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAlso, the argument about black women wearing wigs and weaves as cultural appropriation is a little thin. I believe the culture adopted Caucasian hair texture as a means of survival, not the adoption of style. A good number of black women still feel the scars of European hair texture being more acceptable, and there is still much work to be done around the acceptance of natural Black hair texture. A means of blending in to relieve the pressure of standing out isn&#x2019;t cultural appropriation; it&#x2019;s cultural adaptation. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile we invite others to celebrate our culture with us, we don&#x2019;t want other cultures to take it from us. I hope we can get to a time where Black girls can sport the same hairstyle as Jenner without being followed in a store or feeling as if they&#x2019;re inciting violence or inappropriate attention. I believe that we can all share in the creation of beauty &#x2014; and that includes white women sporting cornrows &#x2014; as long as there&#x2019;s an attempt to benefit the community of origin. Admiration and love of a culture is amazing, but we must stop pirating other people&#x2019;s ideas as our own. We need to respect that beauty is only skin deep, but that as a culture our wounds run all the way to the core. There is much healing to be done, and it can start with giving credit where it&#x2019;s due.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca Consumer Reports Study: Your Sunscreen May Not Work","summary":"Find out which sunscreens you should use and which to avoid.(Photo: David Burton\u002FTrunk Archive) In an alarming new study by Consumer Reports, one third of sunscreens tested didnt offer the protection promised on their labels.  Of the two that did meet their SPF claim, neither received enough high scores to be recommended including California Baby Super Sensitive SPF 30+, and Goddess Garden Organics Sunny Body Natural 30.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fb0f1f48daa6e8bd763488cd28b3a10aa6ed7ad80.jpg\" alt=\"Alarming Consumer Reports Study: Your Sunscreen May Not Work\" width=\"540\" height=\"698\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EFind out which sunscreens you should use and which to avoid.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E(\u003Ci\u003EPhoto: David Burton\u002FTrunk Archive)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn an alarming new study by \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.consumerreports.org\u002Fcro\u002Fsunscreens.htm\"\u003EConsumer Reports\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, one third of sunscreens tested didn&#x2019;t offer the protection promised on their labels. Out of the 34 sunscreens put to the test, 11 failed to meet their SPF and water-resistant claims. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe watchdog group focused particularly on how sunscreens hold up against UVA and UVB rays after they have been exposed to water. They sampled a wide range of price points from drugstore brands to fancy European suncare. To see how the sunscreens held up, they were applied to tester&#x2019;s backs, and submerged in water for the amount of time that the sunscreen promised to hold up. For example, if the product claimed to be waterproof for an hour, that is how long testers would stay drenched. &#xA0;Afterwards testers were exposed to an ultra violet light to determine the effectiveness of the product against the sun&#x2019;s rays. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe 11 sunscreens that didn&#x2019;t live up to expectations missed their target by anywhere from 16% to 70%. Interestingly, 8 of the 11 had an SPF below 30. While it&#x2019;s clear an SPF 30 or above is a good target to look for, don&#x2019;t be fooled into thinking SPFs of 50 or above is always going to add a ton of protection. Several of the high SPF products don&#x2019;t offer as much SPF as they claim. Coppertone ClearlySheer for Beach &amp; Pool SPF 50+ tested as an SPF 37, and Banana Boat Sport Performance with Powerstay Technology SPF 100 tested as an SPF 36.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe other red flag brought up by the study was about natural sunscreens, pointing out that the word &#x201C;natural&#x201D; means nothing on a label. They do acknowledge that it is often used to refer to products that contain zinc oxide and\u002For titanium dioxide as active ingredients. Consumer Reports states that &#x201C;so-called naturals are less likely to offer skin the complete protection it needs.&#x201D; They tested five mineral sunscreens and three failed. Of the two that did meet their SPF claim, neither received enough high scores to be recommended including California Baby Super Sensitive SPF 30+, and Goddess Garden Organics Sunny Body Natural 30. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHowever, while the study is alarming, it&#x2019;s worth noting that the test was really focused on how sunscreens hold up in water, which may not be a fair test. &#x201C;Given that we tell people to reapply sunscreen when coming out of the water, you should look at this study with caution,&#x201D; says Manhattan-based dermatologist Dr. Sejal Shah. Ultimately, the study should be a reminder that sunscreen alone, isn&#x2019;t the best protection. &#x201C;If you are going in the water wear a rash guard. If you are outside, wear sun protective clothing, a hat, and sunglasses too,&#x201D; explains dermatologist Dr. Ava Shamban. &#x201C;Remember, sunscreen is not the end all be all. Don&#x2019;t stop using it, but use other forms of protection too.&#x201D; \u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHere are the sunscreens that earned the top ratings:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E1. La Roche-Posay Anthelios 60 Melt-in Sunscreen Milk, SPF 60. \u003Cbr\u003E2. Vichy Capital Soleil 50 Lightweight Foaming Lotion, SPF 50\u003Cbr\u003E3. Coppertone Water Babies SPF 50\u003Cbr\u003E4. Equate Ultra Protection, SPF 50\u003Cbr\u003E5. No-Ad Sport SPF 50\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHere are the sunscreens that earned the lowest ratings: \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E1.
